CHAPTER I.
	1.0045069902274852

	nan

	nan
It is a truth universally acknowledged, that a single man in possession
	1.0719456137544061
of a good fortune, must be in want of a wife.
	1.0703796837074193

	nan
However little known the feelings or views of such a man may be on his
	1.1013630140245283
first entering a neighbourhood, this truth is so well fixed in the minds
	1.073211473525995
of the surrounding families, that he is considered as the rightful
	1.066260516163524
property of some one or other of their daughters.
	0.0

	nan
"My dear Mr. Bennet," said his lady to him one day, "have you heard that
	1.1011125702318487
Netherfield Park is let at last?"
	1.0272278927620468

	nan
Mr. Bennet replied that he had not.
	1.0482293403407437

	nan
"But it is," returned she; "for Mrs. Long has just been here, and she
	1.097839473361709
told me all about it."
	1.002385408616337

	nan
Mr. Bennet made no answer.
	1.0366972728586288

	nan
"Do not you want to know who has taken it?" cried his wife impatiently.
	1.0874217540882332

	nan
"_You_ want to tell me, and I have no objection to hearing it."
	1.0871137727042788

	nan
This was invitation enough.
	1.0150387440061102

	nan
"Why, my dear, you must know, Mrs. Long says that Netherfield is taken
	1.0831953388286517
by a young man of large fortune from the north of England; that he came
	1.1014543345694998
down on Monday in a chaise and four to see the place, and was so much
	1.0823293595664247
delighted with it that he agreed with Mr. Morris immediately; that he is
	1.076586116050303
to take possession before Michaelmas, and some of his servants are to be
	1.0833256836657998
in the house by the end of next week."
	1.0624144782136795

	nan
"What is his name?"
	1.0120159653125875

	nan
"Bingley."
	nan

	nan
"Is he married or single?"
	1.0159478148039565

	nan
"Oh! single, my dear, to be sure! A single man of large fortune; four
	1.0816648418327417
or five thousand a year. What a fine thing for our girls!"
	1.0735610712293833

	nan
"How so? how can it affect them?"
	1.030410984106126

	nan
"My dear Mr. Bennet," replied his wife, "how can you be so tiresome! You
	1.0878821062901571
must know that I am thinking of his marrying one of them."
	1.0687825223802445

	nan
"Is that his design in settling here?"
	1.0317709714374539

	nan
"Design! nonsense, how can you talk so! But it is very likely that he
	1.0823743762902112
_may_ fall in love with one of them, and therefore you must visit him as
	1.0575763654446928
soon as he comes."
	0.9958876276023131

	nan
"I see no occasion for that. You and the girls may go, or you may send
	1.113638236806335
them by themselves, which perhaps will be still better, for as you are
	1.0626787621439793
as handsome as any of them, Mr. Bingley might like you the best of the
	1.0946783392657033
party."
	nan

	nan
"My dear, you flatter me. I certainly _have_ had my share of beauty, but
	1.0810827508228842
I do not pretend to be any thing extraordinary now. When a woman has
	1.0966035597053405
five grown up daughters, she ought to give over thinking of her own
	1.0734002216488336
beauty."
	nan

	nan
"In such cases, a woman has not often much beauty to think of."
	1.0912938562312486

	nan
"But, my dear, you must indeed go and see Mr. Bingley when he comes into
	1.0977027594384068
the neighbourhood."
	1.0074523372036341

	nan
"It is more than I engage for, I assure you."
	1.065555021289632

	nan
"But consider your daughters. Only think what an establishment it would
	1.06914748278912
be for one of them. Sir William and Lady Lucas are determined to go,
	1.0905542645005228
merely on that account, for in general you know they visit no new
	1.0502227465633185
comers. Indeed you must go, for it will be impossible for _us_ to visit
	1.0908326646083821
him, if you do not."
	1.0089219813517074

	nan
"You are over scrupulous surely. I dare say Mr. Bingley will be very
	1.0956502851552086
glad to see you; and I will send a few lines by you to assure him of my
	1.0837759284706914
hearty consent to his marrying which ever he chuses of the girls; though
	1.0680044737579792
I must throw in a good word for my little Lizzy."
	1.0696896280786574

	nan
"I desire you will do no such thing. Lizzy is not a bit better than the
	1.1141311209170632
others; and I am sure she is not half so handsome as Jane, nor half so
	1.0780888807912983
good humoured as Lydia. But you are always giving _her_ the
	1.0469410518733442
preference."
	nan

	nan
"They have none of them much to recommend them," replied he; "they are
	1.0724603407333089
all silly and ignorant like other girls; but Lizzy has something more of
	1.0723523807988447
quickness than her sisters."
	0.9952177570954321

	nan
"Mr. Bennet, how can you abuse your own children in such a way? You take
	1.1041741891930954
delight in vexing me. You have no compassion on my poor nerves."
	1.0716075308701685

	nan
"You mistake me, my dear. I have a high respect for your nerves. They
	1.096031314861933
are my old friends. I have heard you mention them with consideration
	1.0682042800860854
these twenty years at least."
	0.9959775818792026

	nan
"Ah! you do not know what I suffer."
	1.0421550469472465

	nan
"But I hope you will get over it, and live to see many young men of four
	1.1072522210604157
thousand a year come into the neighbourhood."
	1.0371633316626443

	nan
"It will be no use to us, if twenty such should come since you will not
	1.101362929107576
visit them."
	0.9932849106877489

	nan
"Depend upon it, my dear, that when there are twenty, I will visit them
	1.0783581115368361
all."
	nan

	nan
Mr. Bennet was so odd a mixture of quick parts, sarcastic humour,
	1.0864279457498025
reserve, and caprice, that the experience of three and twenty years had
	1.0607557447995564
been insufficient to make his wife understand his character. _Her_ mind
	1.0611886016543717
was less difficult to develope. She was a woman of mean understanding,
	1.0762376658863473
little information, and uncertain temper. When she was discontented she
	1.0473661561602512
fancied herself nervous. The business of her life was to get her
	1.0573370188652687
daughters married; its solace was visiting and news.
	1.0265127732919286

	nan

	nan

	nan

CHAPTER II.
	1.0045069902274852

	nan

	nan
Mr. Bennet was among the earliest of those who waited on Mr. Bingley. He
	1.121050317672837
had always intended to visit him, though to the last always assuring his
	1.0727947525792405
wife that he should not go; and till the evening after the visit was
	1.0746702366181584
paid, she had no knowledge of it. It was then disclosed in the following
	1.0831154380804557
manner. Observing his second daughter employed in trimming a hat, he
	1.0577574423396
suddenly addressed her with,
	0.9918160206992798

	nan
"I hope Mr. Bingley will like it Lizzy."
	1.0558252840131241

	nan
"We are not in a way to know _what_ Mr. Bingley likes," said her mother
	1.1053217295007374
resentfully, "since we are not to visit."
	1.021370135242019

	nan
"But you forget, mama," said Elizabeth, "that we shall meet him at the
	1.0729488648624146
assemblies, and that Mrs. Long has promised to introduce him."
	1.061579178296081

	nan
"I do not believe Mrs. Long will do any such thing. She has two nieces
	1.117550988064144
of her own. She is a selfish, hypocritical woman, and I have no opinion
	1.0996638895412176
of her."
	1.0040818234041304

	nan
"No more have I," said Mr. Bennet; "and I am glad to find that you do
	1.11388784267393
not depend on her serving you."
	1.0305579921170345

	nan
Mrs. Bennet deigned not to make any reply; but unable to contain
	1.0828871682345371
herself, began scolding one of her daughters.
	1.0181581290328723

	nan
"Don't keep coughing so, Kitty, for heaven's sake! Have a little
	1.0821589804288911
compassion on my nerves. You tear them to pieces."
	1.0423321553396256

	nan
"Kitty has no discretion in her coughs," said her father; "she times
	1.0746285752216984
them ill."
	0.9961511122947492

	nan
"I do not cough for my own amusement," replied Kitty fretfully.
	1.068115047718697

	nan
"When is your next ball to be, Lizzy?"
	1.043744380432309

	nan
"To-morrow fortnight."
	1.0101708178312803

	nan
"Aye, so it is," cried her mother, "and Mrs. Long does not come back
	1.0963927170741619
till the day before; so, it will be impossible for her to introduce him,
	1.0779758179609369
for she will not know him herself."
	1.0332526986966644

	nan
"Then, my dear, you may have the advantage of your friend, and introduce
	1.0771561647368544
Mr. Bingley to _her_."
	1.0288707712921275

	nan
"Impossible, Mr. Bennet, impossible, when I am not acquainted with him
	1.0729001953772976
myself; how can you be so teazing?"
	1.0180870514506255

	nan
"I honour your circumspection. A fortnight's acquaintance is certainly
	1.0664735996376957
very little. One cannot know what a man really is by the end of a
	1.113789859592339
fortnight. But if _we_ do not venture, somebody else will; and after
	1.0636611291079712
all, Mrs. Long and her nieces must stand their chance; and therefore, as
	1.0853290296756346
she will think it an act of kindness, if you decline the office, I will
	1.0900669014531446
take it on myself."
	1.00059474475245

	nan
The girls stared at their father. Mrs. Bennet said only, "Nonsense,
	1.0799886547260962
nonsense!"
	nan

	nan
"What can be the meaning of that emphatic exclamation?" cried he. "Do
	1.0758751366846881
you consider the forms of introduction, and the stress that is laid on
	1.076166812717413
them, as nonsense? I cannot quite agree with you _there_. What say you,
	1.07222258105643
Mary? for you are a young lady of deep reflection I know, and read great
	1.092973948560513
books, and make extracts."
	1.0008501328368753

	nan
Mary wished to say something very sensible, but knew not how.
	1.0690296589623125

	nan
"While Mary is adjusting her ideas," he continued, "let us return to Mr.
	1.0863807822569544
Bingley."
	nan

	nan
"I am sick of Mr. Bingley," cried his wife.
	1.0625967182028175

	nan
"I am sorry to hear _that_; but why did not you tell me so before? If I
	1.0959758008336018
had known as much this morning, I certainly would not have called on
	1.0705414210347532
him. It is very unlucky; but as I have actually paid the visit, we
	1.0839694399776811
cannot escape the acquaintance now."
	1.0018376840374

	nan
The astonishment of the ladies was just what he wished; that of Mrs.
	1.0830566711069405
Bennet perhaps surpassing the rest; though when the first tumult of joy
	1.0795659941991471
was over, she began to declare that it was what she had expected all the
	1.0836347087738263
while.
	nan

	nan
"How good it was in you, my dear Mr. Bennet! But I knew I should
	1.1033082171802464
persuade you at last. I was sure you loved your girls too well to
	1.0766839077355366
neglect such an acquaintance. Well, how pleased I am! and it is such a
	1.0824701913102168
good joke, too, that you should have gone this morning, and never said
	1.0636772483792942
a word about it till now."
	1.0291256750527702

	nan
"Now, Kitty, you may cough as much as you chuse," said Mr. Bennet; and,
	1.0855542133859781
as he spoke, he left the room, fatigued with the raptures of his wife.
	1.0955133965683927

	nan
"What an excellent father you have, girls," said she, when the door was
	1.0745041008040057
shut. "I do not know how you will ever make him amends for his kindness;
	1.0845940286978377
or me either, for that matter. At our time of life, it is not so
	1.090166279841066
pleasant I can tell you, to be making new acquaintance every day; but
	1.0650935038750118
for your sakes, we would do any thing. Lydia, my love, though you _are_
	1.0905235797654573
the youngest, I dare say Mr. Bingley will dance with you at the next
	1.0941759298806557
ball."
	nan

	nan
"Oh!" said Lydia stoutly, "I am not afraid; for though I _am_ the
	1.080158399868753
youngest, I'm the tallest."
	1.0083071314105223

	nan
The rest of the evening was spent in conjecturing how soon he would
	1.074727030633687
return Mr. Bennet's visit, and determining when they should ask him to
	0.0
dinner.

CHAPTER III.
	1.0045069902274852

	nan

	nan
Not all that Mrs. Bennet, however, with the assistance of her five
	1.0858324611290824
daughters, could ask on the subject was sufficient to draw from her
	1.0541612497313642
husband any satisfactory description of Mr. Bingley. They attacked him
	1.0686372834295261
in various ways; with barefaced questions, ingenious suppositions, and
	1.046146129472534
distant surmises; but he eluded the skill of them all; and they were at
	1.0797143993243463
last obliged to accept the second-hand intelligence of their neighbour
	1.0462535910893485
Lady Lucas. Her report was highly favourable. Sir William had been
	1.0841927060044207
delighted with him. He was quite young, wonderfully handsome, extremely
	1.054985760081873
agreeable, and to crown the whole, he meant to be at the next assembly
	1.0852537518511516
with a large party. Nothing could be more delightful! To be fond of
	1.0837056208278553
dancing was a certain step towards falling in love; and very lively
	1.0596595638511668
hopes of Mr. Bingley's heart were entertained.
	1.0402398817788157

	nan
"If I can but see one of my daughters happily settled at Netherfield,"
	1.0760234204951606
said Mrs. Bennet to her husband, "and all the others equally well
	1.0794288459008134
married, I shall have nothing to wish for."
	1.043777466499447

	nan
In a few days Mr. Bingley returned Mr. Bennet's visit, and sat about ten
	1.1210594089811585
minutes with him in his library. He had entertained hopes of being
	1.0745161797090335
admitted to a sight of the young ladies, of whose beauty he had heard
	1.0833307489145567
much; but he saw only the father. The ladies were somewhat more
	1.0644569384976788
fortunate, for they had the advantage of ascertaining from an upper
	1.0557289579957383
window, that he wore a blue coat and rode a black horse.
	1.0781704164404131

	nan
An invitation to dinner was soon afterwards dispatched; and already had
	1.0578018510024094
Mrs. Bennet planned the courses that were to do credit to her
	1.0866686626504138
housekeeping, when an answer arrived which deferred it all. Mr. Bingley
	1.0607950528364058
was obliged to be in town the following day, and consequently unable to
	1.0750989026769655
accept the honour of their invitation, &c. Mrs. Bennet was quite
	1.0753752961773224
disconcerted. She could not imagine what business he could have in town
	0.0
so soon after his arrival in Hertfordshire; and she began to fear that
	1.0760783184367173
he might be always flying about from one place to another, and never
	1.066040041493103
settled at Netherfield as he ought to be. Lady Lucas quieted her fears a
	1.074987276761589

	1.104003131639864

	1.0355431342389048

	1.089567575861906

	1.0801703917193262

	1.0647116167216109

	1.086712201462823
the party entered the assembly room, it consisted of only five
	1.0704829068986286
altogether; Mr. Bingley, his two sisters, the husband of the eldest, and
	1.077083457643519
another young man.
	0.9972317699672536

	nan
Mr. Bingley was good looking and gentleman-like; he had a pleasant
	1.0779786520055752
countenance, and easy, unaffected manners. His sisters were fine women,
	1.0504990591938073
with an air of decided fashion. His brother-in-law, Mr. Hurst, merely

	1.073640004235441

	1.0801571868594442

	1.0574645570179098

	1.0655994972631004

	1.0909880904008808

	1.0541282827941747

	1.0454025014151114
which turned the tide of his popularity; for he was discovered to be
	1.0730800600739696
proud, to be above his company, and above being pleased; and not all his
	0.0

	0.0

	1.0453103398306824

	1.0099955436356602

	nan
Mr. Bingley had soon made himself acquainted with all the principal
	1.0713609613515716

	1.0582727092144146

	1.077613605643306

	1.037847185869041

	1.087088749105547

	1.0731841438770526

	1.0860432635828516

	1.0588792472466713
His character was decided. He was the proudest, most disagreeable man in
	1.0825084565097056

	1.088069541811667

	1.0062658449910225

	1.0808102569668696

	1.0678710212009586

	1.1033205772361394

	1.0053301066107319

"I certainly shall not. You know how I detest it, unless I am
	1.0851307368801064

	0.9963619384273411

	nan
"I would not be so fastidious as you are," cried Bingley, "for a

	1.075214995214335

	1.0237812499497603

	1.0045069902274852

	nan

	nan
Had Elizabeth's opinion been all drawn from her own family, she could
	1.0817836581293134

	0.0

	1.0660891921396853

	1.0528221116223275

	1.058046076835186

	1.0832800804408362

	1.099557214770463

	1.038722399013547

	1.0527475925856324

	1.0655694812836787

	1.0045069902274852

	nan

	1.0626922830735626

	1.070423013247207

	1.0487465855320715
